  30. ***Updated everything, deleted old recommendations and added new products<br />I bought the Gelish kit when it was on major sale at a beauty supply. I also bought a collection of polish colors. If I knew THEN how long-lasting a gel manicure is, I would not have amassed such a huge collection of regular polish! The gel manicures ROCK! [Update: Youtube &#34;Gelly Sandwich&#34; for videos on how to use regular polish with gel for quick-change color]<br />When you first get this kit, don't be shocked at how tiny everything is. I was really ticked off at first (because I didn't read specifics when I bought it, thought I was getting full size products) but this is truly an intro-sized kit. Don't be alarmed though, as there is plenty of product in the kit to get you through MANY manicures! I do both fingers and toes and the kit lasted a long time. You'll use different amounts of products at a different pace, so just buy the components separately as you run out. You'll even find some items are not truly necessary. Some people say there is enough product for 10-12 manicures but I got way, way more than that.<br />You might find the instructions overwhelming at first, I would recommend you Youtube some instructional videos. There are hundreds of how-to videos on not only the basics of the gel manicure, but also special effects like french tips and nail art. You will be amazed at all you can do with the gel! Once you see the steps in action it makes reading through and utilizing the instruction manual much easier. Some kits have a mini-dvd; good luck with *that* thing. There are curing times listed on the back of the box. (Curing times are different with different brands and colors, be prepared)<br />You'll need, in addition to the kit: a UV or LED lamp, lint free nail polish removal pads, a microfine buffer, 70% alcohol would also be good. Updated note: SHAKE YOUR GEL POLISH WELL--all brands--before each use!<br /><br />UPDATED LAMP NOTES: (SAVE YOURSELF THE HASSLE GET THE GELISH LIGHT) I first bought a 32w UV light to use with this instead of the 9w that was sold by the place I got the Gelish set from. The 32w seemed to make the steps work in the amount of time suggested in the Gelish instructions. My first attempt, with the lower wattage 9v UV light, created some problems with bubbling and lifting. You might want to buy a tube of broad-spectrum SPF hand cream also if you are concerned about the effects of the lamp on your skin. There are fingerless gloves sold that help block the rays also.<br />NOTE: I have since found the UV light to be a less economical purchase. Not only does it take longer to process the gel, but you eventually have to replace the bulbs. As the bulbs age, you'll start to notice issues with your nails. Most sites selling UV lamps professionally say you need to change them every 'several years'. That, my friends, is hoo-ha!<br />2015 UPDATE: Just save yourself the money and buy the Gelish light. I made other cheaper lights work but once I got the Gelish light, I stopped having ANY issues whatsoever with any brand. I also use the builder gel (Harmony and IBD) to build my own nails and this light works with those too. Universal success across many brands with one light--NO MORE ISSUES. It's worth the money I promise. Five seconds for your base coat, 20 seconds color coat (regular colors) or 30 seconds dark colors, and 20 to 30 seconds for top coat. This is a lot less than the USpicy light that I used, and I wish now I'd just gotten the Gelish light to begin with. The Gelish lamp does feel pretty warm though, it was a little shocking compared to what I was used to. It also seems to work so quickly that polish doesn't have a chance to spread out like it does in other lamps. IF YOU CAN AFFORD IT GET THE GELISH LAMP TO BEGIN WITH: you will not be sorry.<br />I got SIX WEEKS out of my gel manicure with pale or clear polishes. The interesting thing about the gel is how strong it is, how strong it makes your nails (I had to clip my nails to shorten them, they were so break-proof!). The gel is substantial yet flexible, so it moves with your nails (sometimes we accidentally hit them on things!). This stuff wears off rather than chipping, and after the sixth week I ended up peeling some off. After eight weeks I finally peeled more off, you'll probably need to soak it with acetone to remove it. It peeled off my nails cleanly and with no damage but that was after a long time. When you remove it, your nails are not stunted and weak like they are with acrylic nails. It's well worth the time to do a gel manicure on yourself and if you use a very light color you can go a long, long time without any noticeable dings! (Note, I'm not advocating PEELING it off, but if you have had it on so long that it's ready to give up, that's different. Otherwise you could damage your nails if you peel something that isn't ready to let go yet)<br />NAIL ART: Put the decal on top of your color, before you put on the top coat and cure. The nice thing about gel color, is how STICKY it is, and it's pretty easy to get a decal on without lifting. I don't use the water decals for many reasons (mainly because it wets the gel layer) but you can use them if you have much more patience than I do! The cured top gel layer makes a great sealant on nail art, and it will last and last. I have had mixed results with crystals and add-ons; sometimes if I set them into the top layer before curing, they will stick nicely for weeks. Other times, I look down one day and there is a hole where the crystal/item was. Oops. Regular nail glue on top of cured top coat will still hold them just like regular polish top coat, if you want to try that.<br />TIPS FOR BEST RESULTS:<br />*I get six weeks out of the pale, sheer colors; by the time six weeks have gone by, my nails have grown and there are dings and chinks in the color here and there but since it's the pale, barely-there color, it's hard to tell. If you use any of the bright colors, you can probably get about 2 weeks or so before you either get edge wear or noticeable gap in color from the cuticle due to growth. Once the color starts lifting up and catching your hair at the cuticle edge, that's usually enough to drive you nuts enough to remove it (or buff it down lightly and put on a new top coat)<br /><br />*First, use the nail square buffer to lightly rough the surface of your nails. Don't saw back and forth, stroke it from cuticle to nail tip, lightly. Then take the 'nail cleaner' (or 91% alcohol) product on your lint free cloth and swipe your nails. You don't want any kind of oil on them.<br />*Next you'll use your 'ph bond' product (or skip if you used alcohol)<br />*Then use the foundation product; brush it on THINLY but cover your nail surface. Wrap a little around the tips of your nails too. THINK THIN......<br />*If using a pale/sheer color you can get by with one coat. I like two. THIN THIN THIN, and wrap a little around the tips of your nails.<br />*Top coat, again think thin. But make sure you carefully cover your nail surfaces with it. Don't let it get anywhere else...and don't forget to cap the end of your nail tips a little bit.<br />*Make all coats of product THIN! THIN IS GOOD!<br />*When you use it, avoid letting it get on your cuticles or running down the sides of your nails. If this happens, get an orange stick and take care of it before you set it! And keep in mind, this product DOES spread out a little bit. The best way to guarantee that your polish job will lift and peel off, is to not do thin layers, and to let this get outside of the nail bed.<br />*Make sure to take the time to carefully paint down the sides as far as you can, covering the color coat. This will help it last longer, without the lifting problems that can happen. Sometimes it will make a little sharp 'ledge' if you get sloppy, and this will tend to catch on things. Or if you are like me, it will make you want to pick at it. You can take a buffer or light board and gently sand this ridge down, and do another stripe of top coat if you want to. If you don't, the integrity of your polish job is compromised and it's only a matter of time before it starts to deconstruct. It's up to you!<br /><br />TROUBLESHOOTING:<br />*If you consistently get 'pliable, peely' color, there are several things to consider. 99% of the time, it's going to be that your layers are too thick. Back off on how much you use, it really takes about half of what you think it does. (And the plus side is that it will go farther!)<br />If it's still pliable after you've carefully applied THIN layers, consider that your light may be the culprit. I bought an LED light (look around for best price!) that is large enough for one whole hand; I didn't find the 'portable' lights (especially those that do 4 fingers!!) to be great. I also have UV light but I think that the bulbs are not as effective despite the ridiculous long life claims of the seller I bought them from. (UPDATE: The Gelish light solved every problem I ever had)<br />If you have tried thinner layers, and upping your cure time (try 1 min extra for UV, 30 sec extra for LED) isn't working, consider blaming your foundation coat formula, this was the culprit in my second Gelish kit. UPDATE 8-22-12: I found a bottle of my Gelish base coat that was over a year old, was very thick and kind of gloppy. I used it anyway and am certain this is the culprit for several of my nails just popping off the entire color in one piece, like a fake nail. I tossed the bottle.<br />&#34;IT FEELS LIKE MY NAILS ARE BURNING UP&#34;: I've had this happen a few times with both UV and LED lights. Apparently this is very common. The worst burning I ever experienced was at a salon with Gelish Starburst with UV lamp, I thought it was just the fact that the tech was really putting it on and curing it too long, but this feeling can happen and doesn't signify that you are being burned. Even though it can burn like a biotch! I've had it even with very thin coats. It probably won't happen very often to you but if it does, at least you know it's to be expected. It is a process of the color curing.<br />*If you get color on your wipe when doing the cleansing step on your top coat, this means that not all the nail color was sealed with the top clear coat. It could just be some that ended up outside your nail bed (but I already told you not to let that happen!), but it is also likely there is a side that didn't get all the top coat.<br />FOR LONGER NAILS: You may find that a color isn't as opaque as you like, when on your tips. It is frustrating when you can see light through your nail tips, or see strokes of color as the light shines through! I like to make my first base color coat (THIN!) on the tips, painting horizontally across the ends, and wrapping a little color around the tips. Bake that . Then go for layer 2 and even 3 if you need it, painting from cuticle to tip. I've found this is the best way to get opaque color to the very ends of my nails, especially when they are long, and it has dramatically increased edge wear on my darker colors. It only takes a few extra seconds for a longer color payoff. You won't need more than 2 layers on your nail bed MOST of the time, but the tips are where you need opacity: with this horizontal first-layer method, you can get full color on your tips with no shine-through, and still get by with two coats on your nail bed, which helps stave off bubbling and lifting. I changed my mind about several Gelish polishes I was about to give away because they were so thin that I couldn't be happy with the tips, now that is not a problem. By the time you add another two coats of color plus your top coat, you cannot tell there is a heavier layer on your tips.<br />USING THEM WITH ACRYLIC NAILS: I made the mistake of getting some acrylic nails for a wedding; the guy did a bad job on top of picking tips that make it look like I have Frito Scoops on the ends of my fingers. (Where's the bean dip?!?!?!) Here is how I dealt with that fugly garbage!<br />**As the acrylic nail grows out, you get that space between it and the cuticle, and that HUMP right where the acrylic starts. That's also where you'll get lifting and stuff like your hair getting caught in it UGH. So take that nail dremel and put on the barrel sanding attachment. You'll hold it at an angle and just take that 'hump' of acrylic on that edge, down to where it's NOT to the nail but not still...hump-y. While you are at it, you might run the barrel attachment down the sides, you know how sometimes you get lifting edges down there too? You'll just want to smooth that down. If you got the person who thinks acrylic nails should be an inch thick, then go ahead and lay that barrel parallel to the nail surface and work some of that extra thick acrylic down too, in back and forth motions. No sense in looking like you bring your own Frito chips to the party.<br />*And then just lightly, carefully, rough up the nail bed between the cuticle and acrylic nail area. With your buffer block, NOT THE DREMEL!<br />*I use a lint free wipe to wipe down the area with alcohol, to get the dust off. You can either leave it at that or use the PH Bond. I know a lot of people say oh it's just alcohol (it has something else in it too), but hey if you have the bottle you may as well use it up.<br />*Next is the foundation. I paint it THINLY on the acrylic nail first, and then I start from the cuticle and paint towards the acrylic nail to cover the new growth area. I found that if you have had some lifting at the edge, this helps make a nice seal.<br />*Then you can either do a color coat here at this step; if you do color, do a couple of THIN THIN layers, but this time stroke the color from cuticle to nail tip, one long stroke each time, so you don't get color pooling at the front edge of the acrylic. Wrap a little bit of the color around the ends of the acrylic tips too<br />*next you do the top coat, again one long stroke each time, and make sure to wrap it around the ends a little. Just helps make it look good longer<br />If you use a sheer color you can pretty much make the acrylic nails invisible with this method, or something light. I found that a bright color emphasized the `hump' area, but the lighter colors made the acrylic and real nail appear pretty seamless. You'll be surprised once you do all the layers, how even the whole thing looks! The gel polish fills in the gap between your new nail growth and the acrylic. It took me several months but I eventually got to the point that when I clipped my nails to shorten them one day, the acrylic was so far to the tips of my nails that it just broke off. Voila, no weak soggy breaking nails! *OH one thing I forgot to mention: if you ever see darkness or discoloring under your nails as you are growing these out, remove your acrylic! It's probably fungal growth and you need to get that acrylic off!<br />(NEW) BUILDER GEL: You can use IBD or Harmony Builder Gel to fill in your growth. You'll need the ProBond IBD and IBD Bonder (superior to Gelish) no matter which brand you buy. The process is more complicated and I'd recommend some Youtube videos. It takes a bit of practice but is amazingly easy and you can get the supplies for less than the cost of a fill in at the salon.<br />*if you soak off the gel, the product used to soak off the gel will also affect the integrity of your acrylic nail. I left my gel on so long that it just peeled off after about six weeks (what was left of it, ha!) but you can lightly buff the clear off and do a thin color overcoat and another top coat if using the same color.<br />VOGUE PROFESSIONAL (r) Rechargeable Cordless Nail Drill File Acrylics Gels Natural Nails Salon Pedicure Pro is the nail dremel I bought, and I am very happy with it.<br /><br />PRODUCT COMPATIBILITY:<br />*I deleted the Red Carpet paragraph because I just found it to be worthless. Yes there are folks who like it but I'm getting such pretty results with better products.<br />*LOMASI: They are hard to find so I stopped using them. They are compatible with Gelish base and top coat. They are pretty opaque and worth buying if you find them.<br />*PROGEL: deleted this paragraph because they aren't worth two cents.<br />*SHELLAC/CND: I bought &#34;Strawberry Smoothie&#34; and at first was annoyed that the bottle did not seem to match the picture. This is very sheer, and the photo online appeared to be a frosty pink. However, after using it, and achieving what seems like the perfect neutral go with anything nail, I love this. I love how the Shellac applies, how it cures, and how it wears. (Warning, it does smell like normal nail polish until you cure it!) I love how absolutely rock-hard and glassy it feels. I never wonder, wow did I cure this properly?? It is compatible with Gelish top and foundation coats. It cures flawlessly in the Gelish light. Darker colors often need 30 seconds cure.<br />*IBD: I was hesitant to try them because they are so inexpensive (I often get them for $5 to $6) Zero problems with opacity or application. The decorative topcoats (unlike Gelish) most often provide the PUNCH you are looking for with one coat. Completely compatible with Gelish top and foundation. I find I have to cure them 30 seconds each coat with the Gelish light. Honestly I prefer IBD over Gelish for their brush, application, durability, and opacity.<br />So at the end of the day if I had to rank all these products in order of preference, with QUALITY and ease of use being the factors (not price):<br />*IBD and Gelish would share the top spot for application, endurance, some Gelish has opacity problems but just follow my trick for the horizontal tip-painting and see how that works for you. I love IBD hands-down over any other brand right now for ease of use, fewest number of coats, and the fact it's half the price or less of Gelish.<br />*Shellac and Lomasi are hardly in my rotation because they are pricier (Lomasi hard to find) and I've had some brush stroke issues with satin Shellac colors.<br />*Red Carpet, Progel NEVERed. It is a process of the color curing. *If you get color on your wipe when doing the cleansing step on your top coat, this means that not all the nail color was sealed with the top clear coat. It could just be some that ended up outside your nail bed (but I already told you not to let that happen!), but it is also likely there is a side that didn't get all the top coat. FOR LONGER NAILS: You may find that a color isn't as opaque as you like, when on your tips. It is frustrating when you can see light through your nail tips, or see strokes of color as the light shines through! I like to make my first base color coat (THIN!) on the tips, painting horizontally across the ends, and wrapping a little color around the tips. Bake that . Then go for layer 2 and even 3 if you need it, painting from cuticle to tip. I've found this is the best way to get opaque color to the very ends of my nails, especially when they are long, and it has dramatically increased edge wear on my darker colors. It only takes a few extra seconds for a longer color payoff. You won't need more than 2 layers on your nail bed MOST of the time, but the tips are where you need opacity: with this horizontal first-layer method, you can get full color on your tips with no shine-through, and still get by with two coats on your nail bed, which helps stave off bubbling and lifting. I changed my mind about several Gelish polishes I was about to give away because they were so thin that I couldn't be happy with the tips, now that is not a problem. By the time you add another two coats of color plus your top coat, you cannot tell there is a heavier layer on your tips. USING THEM WITH ACRYLIC NAILS: I made the mistake of getting some acrylic nails for a wedding; the guy did a bad job on top of picking tips that make it look like I have Frito Scoops on the ends of my fingers. (Where's the bean dip?!?!?!) Here is how I dealt with that fugly garbage! **As the acrylic nail grows out, you get that space between it and the cuticle, and that HUMP right where the acrylic starts. That's also where you'll get lifting and stuff like your hair getting caught in it UGH. So take that nail dremel and put on the barrel sanding attachment. You'll hold it at an angle and just take that 'hump' of acrylic on that edge, down to where it's NOT to the nail but not still...hump-y. While you are at it, you might run the barrel attachment down the sides, you know how sometimes you get lifting edges down there too? You'll just want to smooth that down. If you got the person who thinks acrylic nails should be an inch thick, then go ahead and lay that barrel parallel to the nail surface and work some of that extra thick acrylic down too, in back and forth motions. No sense in looking like you bring your own Frito chips to the party. *And then just lightly, carefully, rough up the nail bed between the cuticle and acrylic nail area. One key to making the manicure last is getting a good coat on the free edge of the nail, and that wasn't easy with my first couple of times because my nails were short. So the first couple times didn't last as long. The free edge starts to wear first, and then the polish can lift and peel. It's also important to not run the products up on the cuticle, as that is another place for it to lift and peel.<br /><br />The only negative I can say I have with this system is the time factor, I guess. When you put on the top coat, cure it, and cleanse your nails, you are done. No guarding the polish til it gets fully hard, it's good to go. Soaking off the old polish, filing, cleaning, takes me a minimum of 30 minutes, base coat, top coat, two coats of polish and curing time between. Plus, I use two coats of the structure gel as I felt the polish alone just wasn't tough enough for my hard working hands. I already had a one bulb UV light that I can carefully put both hands in at the same time, but I've been going three minutes just to be on the safe side. I may spring for an LED light in the future just to save some time. I guess this is all offset by the fact that I won't have to repeat the process for two weeks if I don't want to.<br /><br />All in all, I am very happy with this product. It's the best thing to come along since the fork. My nails are long, beautiful, strong and natural. Will continue to use it and order from this seller who is very prompt.

  97. I have been doing my own gel nails for almost 3 years. I have tried a few different brands and always find myself coming back to Gelish. It lasts longer than other brands I’ve tried and is a great price. Doing your own gel nails has a bit of a learning curve. I’m guessing you’re looking at this set because you’re wanting to try it out. I’ll say off the bat that Gelish is great. This kit gives you nearly everything you need to get started (minus a light and color). The mini bottles last long enough to get you through more 20 manicures in my experience, so for $1-2 a manicure, this is a wonderful deal.<br /><br />Here are the basic steps to doing your own manicure:<br />1. File and clip nails to your desired length. If you plan on leaving the polish on for 2 weeks, go slightly shorter since they will grow quite a bit.<br />2. Buff the nails well. Especially the creases and up by the cuticile. I like using a buffer block, it gets in the creases better. If the nail is still smooth and shiny it will probably lift early.<br />3. Wash hands and allow to dry fully. Moisture in the nails will be trapped by the polish and shorten the life of your manicure.<br />4. Use cleaner in lint free wipe to clean nail. I use an alcohol pad for this step.<br />5. Use the pH bond. It’s thin and watery. It takes about 30 seconds to soak in.<br />6. Apply foundation. This is the thickest of all the polish. Make sure not to get any on the skin, if you do use the stick to wipe it off before curing! Cap the nail, meaning put a little polish on the edge.<br />7. Cure under light for the required amount of time. It’s 5 seconds with my Gelish light.<br />8. Paint a coat of color, putting some the edge. Again, make sure not to get any on the nail or cuticle, but get as close as you can.<br />9. Cure for required amount of time. Mine is 20-30 seconds. Paint another coat, cure again. Do this until you have the coverage you want.<br />10. Apply top coat. This is the one that is the thinnest. I used to always get it pooled in the creases between my skin because I put too much on. Wipe the brush off well and apply a thin coat.<br />11. Cure under light. Its 30 seconds with the Gelish light.<br />12. Wipe down with either alcohol wipe or the cleanser.<br /><br />Just to save you a little time, here are a few things I learned over the years:<br /><br />• Practice: Practice makes perfect. Don’t get discouraged if your first few manicures turn out bad. I took pictures of my first couple and they look pretty horrid. There’s polish pooled on the sides, my cuticles are covered in polish, the layers are uneven. Now my friends are amazed that my nails I did at home look as good as theirs that they spend a lot of money on. Doing my right hand took quite some time, but now I’ve developed great fine motor control and it looks perfect. Practicing on friends or fake nails is a great also. I have fake nails I use to practice designs on.<br />• LED: I initially bought a UV light that fit both hands for about $50, I used it for over 2 years. I recently bought a Gelish LED light for about $200. I’m so mad I didn’t buy it earlier. Yes, it is expensive, but compared to my friends who get their manicures at a salon for $30+ it’s absolutely worth it. Say I do my nails every 2 weeks for 2 years, that’s 52 manicures. At $30 a piece, which is a very conservative estimate, that’s $1,560 in manicures. I do Gelish pedicures on myself as well, so that increases the savings by a lot. Spend the extra money to get a nice light! I’ve invested about $400 in my gel nails with the lights, a variety of colors and a couple sets of Gelish top/base coat. It’s been worth every penny. I can do my base coat in 5 seconds and other coats in 30 seconds. I also experiment around more with designs now since the process is so quick. I also don’t mind fixing just one nail since it only takes a couple minutes with the LED.<br />• Prep: Your manicure will only be as goodas the prep you do on your nail. This includes taking off all the old polish, filing the nails to a nice length (they will grow over 2 weeks so go slightly shorter than you want), a good buffing and letting your nails dry well. I used to not prep my nails good enough and that was another reason they weren’t lasting as long as they should.<br />• Time: Set aside a big block of time to do it, rushing through will not give you the nice finished product you want. Make sure you’re comfortable with your painting elbow supported. Find a good TV show or put on some music. Make sure all your supplies are handy, including some paper towels and the sticks to get in the cracks. Don’t do it after drinking a ton of coffee (made that mistake and was too jittery).<br />• Cap the edges: This is one part of the whole process that it took me awhile to appreciate. I never knew why my nails lifted at the tips so quickly. I wasn’t putting polish on the free edge and as I did tasks the gel at the edge slowly started lifting. When you put a little polish on the edge it seals it. I do this by painting a nail, when I’m done with that nail my brush doesn’t have much polish on it. I run it along the edge, since it doesn’t have much polish it’s a thin later, then I redip it in the bottle and finish that nail I just “capped”. This prevents me from having a bulge at the tip, like you get if you cap the nail after painting it.<br />• Complete kit versus basics: This kit has more products than you absolutely need. Realistically, you could just buy the pH bond, foundation and top it off. The bottle of &#34;artificial nail remover&#34; is the same (or similar) to acetone remover, the bottle of &#34;Nail surface cleanse&#34; can be substituted with 70% alcohol wipes and the &#34;Nourish&#34; cuticle oil I’ve never used. This kit has it all and some basic tools .There are Gelish kits for the same price minus all the extras that have full size bottles. I do like the mini bottles because it gets replaced before it ever gets old.<br />• Watch your skin: Pick up a wood stick (a toothpick could probably work) and get everything off your skin and cuticle prior to curing. This will make everything look better and save some you some frustration. Anywhere the polish touches the skin is where it will lift and drive you crazy. When I was using my UV light I did both hands at the same time to save money. It was very hard to get my skin clean and not mess up the paint. I find it much easier now that I do one hand at a time.<br />• Think thin: Thin layers are best. It’s hard to do at first, but it’s better to do 3-4 coats of thin polish rather than 2 coats of thick polish. This will prevent the excess from dripping in the creases, make it cure better and make it look better.<br />• Commitment: Once you get started you will be addicted. I feel like I have to have gel polish on at all times now. Before this my nails were short and ugly. I bit them, peeled them and they weren’t cute at all. Now they are medium length and always kept up beautifully. If I take my polish off and even go a day without it my nails chip and are horrible. Between taking the old nails off and redoing them it’s about an 1 ½ to 2 hour process. I do it about every week and a half religiously. It’s sometimes annoying, but the end result makes it worth it.<br /><br />I've now got to the point where I have started experimenting with nail art and do some of my friends nails. I gave away my UV light to a friend, got her hooked on them and now she bought the Gelish light. This kit is a great way to try it out without a huge commitment. Although I do love my Gelish light, there are smaller, cheaper ones out there if you’re not sure you want spend that much upfront. I do recommend LED though, for health reasons and because it’s so much faster. If you have any questions feel free to ask.as the prep you do on your nail. This will prevent the excess from dripping in the creases, make it cure better and make it look better.<br />• Commitment: Once you get started you will be addicted. Although I do love my Gelish light, there are smaller, cheaper ones out there if you’re not sure you want spend that much upfront. I do recommend LED though, for health reasons and because it’s so much faster. If you have any questions feel free to ask.

You can do a Google search for Harmony Gelish Application. There are a bunch of videos out there that show you how to apply this product. The first time I did my nails it took me two hours. The next time it took 1.5 hours so I am hoping that the third time only takes 1 hour. However, it is well worth spending the time to do the manicure correctly.   134. WAITED TO WRITE THIS REVIEW UNTIL AFTER READING MANY REVIEWERS, WEBSITES AND MONTHS OF TRIAL AND ERROR! I waited to write this review until I had tried MANY of the tips from MANY of the wonderful reviewers on Amazon.com! Below is what has finally worked for me the best. I have been doing my own nails for years .. when I heard how long gel nails lasted .. I was hooked! I find my pedicure will last easily 4 weeks .. my manicure very nicely 2 weeks .. then I must start to \\"tip\\" the ends with a matching regular nail polish. If I am not in a hurry .. the best way is to use an OPI base coat plus the color .. it will last better. My nails grow quickly so I really can't last much longer than 3 weeks without a LOT of regrowth along the cuticle. Hope the below is helpful .. thanks to all the other Reviewers who helped me get started on gel nails! AUGUST 2013 (SORRY IN ADVANCE THAT MY \\"WORD\\" DOCUMENT CONVERTS SO BADLY TO AMAZON VIA THE SENTENCE STRUCTURES!) The motto for GEL is \\"thin to win\\" - several very thin layers, no thick ones! Manicure & Pedicure Gelish Application AUGUST 2013 The motto for GEL is \\"thin to win\\" - several very thin layers, no thick ones. Manicure & Pedicure Gelish Application [...] 1. First remove old gel polish. Rough up nails well so acetone can get through. Then starting with the little finger and work to the thumb. Soak pad of Hands Down with acetone. Start with the short end of Hands Down .. with the pad slightly off center. Pull it tightly over the nail bed, it will settle to the center of the nail bed, keeping full contact with the nail as it soaks the gel off. When 5 fingers complete .. put on a disposable glove. . This helps keep the pads moist longer. Do the second hand. Put a glove on the second hand and set the timer for 20 minutes after completing 2nd hand. With the gloves on, can do other tasks. After 20 minutes, remove the glove and pull off the pads, one at a time .. starting with little finger-1st hand,flipping the polish off each nail with an orange stick as you go. If some sticks on the tips, a little pressure with an orange stick coated with acetone ought to make it release. Pads can reused a couple of times before throwing away .. flick off old polish from pad/flatten/let dry/store separated in paper sheets they came in. (Using: Graham Hands Down Soak Off Gel Nail Wraps-works GREAT! -for small toenails the pad can be cut in half for double usage!) 2. Apply cuticle remover .. push back the cuticle. 3. Remove cuticle from nail plate. Clean up as needed. 4. Shape the natural nail using your 240 grit file of choice. 5. Gently remove the shine using the 100 grit side of a 100/180 Buffer until very smooth. 6. Remove the dust and clean the nail. . (IF POSSIBLE: apply vitamin E oil to your nails and fingers after this process because the acetone is very drying. Leave on overnight if possible. Then: wash with soap and water and polish using the proper steps. 7. Wipe the nail with NAIL PREP (or70/91% alcohol) using a lint free wipe (can even use small cuts of lint free paper towel). Use an orange stick to fully clean around cuticles with the alcohol. You don't want any kind of oil on the nails. 8. Apply PH Bond to the nail plate. (or skip if you used alcohol if you choose) APPLY SPARINGLY - i.e. very thin coat! (Use a dry brush and pull more product OFF the nail to ensure it's thin enough.) . 9. SKIP TO #12 IF nails are not peeling/brittle/weak/damaged. If you have normal nails just using Foundation Gel as your base. **Apply Gelish NAIL STRENGHENER STRENGTH-green bottle .. (instead of GELISH FOUNDATION GEL) - first seal the edges of the nail. If needed apply 2 thin layers of the Gelish strengthener. Place hand in the LED Light for 30 seconds. 10. Apply NAIL STRENGHTENER RECOVERY-gold bottle for added strength and that takes care of most problems.) Place hand in the LED Light for 30 seconds. (This xtra step is only necessary for poor nails!) If you apply too thick a coat, your results will suffer. Place hand in the LED Light for 10 seconds. 10b NEXT .. \\"STRUCTURE GEL. NOTE: dot a small amount of base coat on each nail with the brush. Then, wipe the rest of the gel off of the brush. Use the mostly dry brush to spread the small amount of product on your nail. I even wipe the brush off between each nail. This ensures a thin layer OR WILL PEEL! Place hand in the LED Light for 30 seconds. (This xtra step is only necessary for poor nails but Structure Gel is a wonderful strong product!.) 11. If you choose you can emove some of the tacky surface residue with clean dry brush. DO NOT USE CLEANSER... this is a DRY cleaning. 12. Apply Gelish Color Coat of Choice. First, seal the free edge of the nail. Then, apply to the nail plate in a THIN LIGHT APPLICATION from cuticle to free edge. If you apply too thick a coat, your results will suffer. APPLICATION SHOULD BE ALMOST SEE-THROUGH ON 1st COAT! Place hand in the LED Light for 30 seconds (30 seconds for light colors). (As with ALL UV products, cure thumbs very carefully OR separately for best results. 13. Repeat Step 11, 12 & 13 for 2nd color coat. 14. Apply Gelish Top Coat (GELISH TOP IT OFF GEL SEALER). First seal the free edge. Then, apply from cuticle to free edge using a THIN LIGHT APPLICATION. If you apply too thick a coat, your results will suffer. Place hand in LED Light for 20 seconds. (As with ALL UV products, cure thumbs very carefully OR separately for best results. 15. Wipe off the tacky surface residue with NAIL PREP (or alcohol) using a lint free wipe. 16. Use cuticle oil nightly as this helps keep the product flexible and less prone to cracking. TIPS: a. I find it better to complete one step .. including the LED light .. with one hand at a time because the gel does not dry at all .. causing smudges if I attempt to do the step on the 2nd hand without the LED light. b. I use a narrow orange stick and an old cleaned polish bottle filled with acetone to remove any gel touching a cuticle or skin. I do this as I go as it is easier to do while wet .. IMPOSSIBLE after the LED light!c. Peeling: If you have tried thinner layers, and upping your cure time (try 1 min extra for UV, 30 sec extra for LED) isn't working, consider blaming your foundation coat formula, this was the culprit in my second Gelish kit. d. By searching and finally finding a regular nail polish (Sally Hansen \\"#350 Heart to Heart\\" Diamond Strength No Chip Nail Color) close to my gel polish (gelish \\"Tiger Blossum-Item #01334) I have been able to make my nails last up to nearly 4 weeks! Not looking great toward the end but tolerable! In the beginning it is merely \\"tipping\\" the nails .. ie using the #350 to color the tip of the nails after they wear off. I find I must do this nearly every day .. just do this as I put on my make up .. being careful of the finger tips as I apply my make up. Then as the gel gets to be 2-3 to 4 weeks old my nail beds have grown out at least 1/4\\". I then carefully add the #350 around the upper nail bed .. then add a regular top coat to make it all shiny. I get another week out of it .. YEAH! e. Purpose: Used to strengthen weak nails OR to equalize the level differences between the natural nail plate and applied false nail tips. Use this product after the Gelish Foundation (BASE) step has been completed Directions: Apply 1-3 thin coats depending upon nail strength desired; curing between each application. When applying, I use a small flat brush and place a dot of gel into the center of my nail. Using a gentle swirling motion I cover the entire nail. You want to minimize the times you lift the brush from the product so as not to incorporate air bubbles. Once the nail is covered with the sculpting gel, turn your hand over keeping it level for 1 minute. This helps the applied gel to self level in a nicely rounded and natural shape. Cure as directed between each application. See requirements for the cure time needed Requirements: Gelish structure must be cured with an LED lamp or UV lamp system. This helps to equal out the level differences between the two. On the third application I cover the entire nail including the false tip. The cotton ball method is cheap and very easy. BUT YOU NEED TO KNOW: a good light (uv or led, it's all about your preference) is important. I had initially bought the 9 watt gelish mini light and it is absolute garbage. It wouldn't cure any of the steps no matter how long I used it.   199. I was so excited to get this kit! Since it didn't come with color gel, I ordered Princess and Sleek White in order to do a French manicure. I had my daughter-n-law do my nails for me. We were both impressed at how easy it was! My nails looked as if I had just been to the salon! Everything arrived as it should. My kit did not come with any instructions, but I went to youtube and we learned from that as to how to do this. We really liked the fact that the base coat (princess) went on first-then under the lamp for 120 secs. Then we put on the sleek white polish. Using non-acetone nail polish remover, with an artist paint brush (we highly recommend a quality paint brush as little hairs can cause issues from other types of brushes--especially those designed for make-up!) we were easily able to shape the smile for the french tips. It removed just the white polish very easily! Then under the lamp for another 120 secs (we used a 36 watt UV curing lamp) We followed this with the top coat (included in the kit) and left it under the lamp for 180 secs. (my lamp has two different timer settings) Using lint-free nail wipes we used the nail surface cleanse (also included in kit) to wipe the nails clean. You can also use alcohol once you run out of this cleanse. You end up with professional looking nails when you are finished. One more tip--be sure to clean any polish off your skin before curing. We used the non-acetone polish remover to do this as it can't remove the polish below that has already been cured. Below are the steps we used: 1. buff nails and shape nails 2. Paint nails with the pH bond 3. Paint nails with the foundation 4. cure under lamp for 120 sec. (If someone is helping you, while one hand was under the lamp, the other hand can be painted. 5. Paint on your base color (Princess, bashful etc.) 6. Cure 120 sec. under lamp 7. Add Sleek White for the french tips (we did 2 coats curing between the coats) . 8. With an artist brush and non acetone polish remover, form the \\"smile\\" for the French tips. Take your time with the first coat and get it exactly how you want it. The second coat will be easier because you now have something to follow. 9. Cure under lamp for 120 sec. (remember--do this with each coat) 10. Paint on the Top if Off Sealer 11. Cure under lamp for 180 secs to make sure it is well cured. 12. Using a lint free nail wipe, clean nails with the Nail Surface Cleanse. This removes the tackiness leaving you with beautiful smooth, sleek, shiny nails! Your beautiful nails should last several weeks. This is only day two for me and already I am impressed because a typical French manicure using regular polish will only last me a day before it starts chipping off. If I can get a week I will be pleased! I gave this 4 stars because I think they should include directions.

  206. If you are new to DIY gel nails the Gelish system is easy. A great system if you can afford a decent 36V UV lamp.<br /><br />It should be noted that I only recommend the Gelish system for people who can paint their nails, with traditional polish, if they can paint neatly. If you are a sloppy nail painter I do not recommend any gel system, as it is unforgiving one you `cook' the polish under the UV lamp.<br /><br />EACH PRODUCT<br /><br />BASE COAT AND TOP COAT<br />The base coat and top coat are what I would consider the only required products in the set. The ingredients are nearly the same. On the box they are EXACTLY the same but on the Amazon product info they vary slightly. The base coat is thicker and the top coat leaves a slightly higher shine. So if you run out of one, and are in a pinch, you can just use one of the products. I did so successfully on 2 occasions.<br /><br />GELISH PH BOND<br />Although not required for the system, it does help people that have a nail chemistry that resists keeping on polish. So if regular polish starts to chip on you, within the first day or two, your nail chemistry will benefit from this product.<br /><br />My personal nail chemistry makes it hard for me to keep on even salon applied solar gel nails on for more than a few days. Gelish nail product does last me about 5 days with minimal micro chips; this is a long time for me. Once I do dishes thought they are ruined since I don't use any dish gloves.<br /><br />GELISH NOURISH<br />This is a similar product put on every time I have ever gone to get a salon manicure. It is helpful to keep cuticles from drying out and maintain a healthy (and healtly looking) cuticle. I find this important more so when using this Gelish system since the gel does dry hard and can irritate cuticle when placed slightly on top of cuticle; and the UV light is a little harsh on skin.<br /><br />GELISH CLENSER<br />This is perfect for wiping of the tacky residue. I use it after base coat and top coat. Be sure to use a lint free cloth. I recommend, to save some money, purchasing some non-acetone polish remover in its place. Non-acetone remover removed my fear of degrading the chemical process.<br /><br />GELISH REMOVER<br />This product works as described. Just soak your nails in product for 30 seconds and remove. I do have to kind of scrape off the product. A more economical replacement is just buying a bottle of pure acetone. It does the trick.

Never let it touch your cuticles as it will peel up in that spot. Get a good \\"cap\\" on the ends of the nails, even if it gets on the skin of your finger tips- that will peel off without effect. 2 minutes in the thermal spa to cure is plenty. If the polish starts to peel at the edges or back, just use a nail clipper to clip it off. To remove, soak in a small amuont of acetone for 10-15 minutes and use a tool to scrape it off.<br /><br />Another cool thing is that you can put regular polish on over the Gelish (one coat is plenty) and take it off with the non-acetone remover with no effect whatsoever on the Gelish. The Foundation base and the Top It Off sealer appear to be nearly exactly the same ingredients listed in the same order. The foundation appears to be a bit thicker than the top coat. All the small bottles with brushes are .30 oz.<br /><br />The Nail Surface Cleanse appears to be mostly Isopropyl Alcohol with some Acetone thrown in. And the Artificial Nail Remover is mostly rose scented Acetone. These two items are in 2 oz bottles with a foil seal under their caps.<br /><br />Years ago, in the early 90's, I bought some type of clear gel product and UV Lamp at a state fair. Worked good but I worried about the repeated use of the UV lamp. It felt very hot. I scared myself out of using it and gave it away. Ten years later I taught myself to do do my own acrylic nails after a bad experience; the manicurist I went to ignored what I was telling him (I have very thin nails) and quickly wore a hole in the middle of my nail with his Dremel while trying to \\"ruff up\\" my nail. It cut the nail bed and he insisted on \\"fixing it\\" by covering it with the acrylic stuff. It bled a great deal and stung worse... I should have walked out after he damaged my nail. One person wrote: \\"Harmony recommends for best performance you use a \\"color\\" layer. Simple Sheer is their basically clear color coat. It has a very slight pink tint, but once it's on your nail you can't tell it's anything but clear.\\" Another person wrote: \\"I just used IBD Superbond, Gelish Foundation and Top-It-Off and it wore like steel.\\"<br /><br />I also ordered the IBD Superbond base and a bottle of the Gelish \\"Simple Sheer\\" in case the base/top coat alone isn't enough. IBD is supposed to be a stronger bonding agent than the Gelish (or any other) base. Those items haven't arrived yet.<br /><br />The cool thing is, once I have the clear gels set, I can paint my nails with regular (non gel) nail polish. The polish is easily removed with NON-acetone remover and won't affect the gel nail underneath. Halloween is coming up and I don't want to be stuck with Halloween nails for 3 weeks after Halloween! I don't know if I do everything by the book, but here is what I do and it works for me:<br /><br />1) pH Bond -- 2 minutes UV light<br />2) Foundation -- 2 minutes UV light<br />3) gel color of your choice -- 2 minutes UV light (repeat for total of 3 coats)<br />4) Top It Off -- 3 minutes UV light<br />5) wipe off with Nail Surface Cleanse -- no UV light<br />6) Nourish the cuticles and surrounding skin -- no UV light<br /><br />Tips: Apply everything in thin coats, and don't get polish on your cuticles or it will lift and peel.<br /><br />Voila.<br /><br />Use the artificial nail remover to remove the polish when done. I recommend a very absorbent cotton, like the type used in disposable powder puffs. Cut them down to size, soak them in the artificial nail remover, put them on the nails and wrap with foil. In a few minutes, you will see it start to crackle. At that point, the polish is easy to remove.<br /><br />This kit is very complete. I'm glad I bought it and not each and every bottle individually. It's easy to use. Just wish the instructions were easier to read.

  309. I recently decided to do my own nails because I couldn't rationalize paying $45+ at the salon every 2 weeks for the same thing. I bought the Salon Edge 36W UV light machine for $25 and this mini kit. I was pretty nervous since I needed to use tips with this and wasn't sure what to expect. Buy their $5 membership card to save even more. They give you a $5 gift certificate to use within 6 weeks. This kit does NOT come with any nail polish. I read several uTube videos that you can use regular nail polish but you have to wait for it to dry before putting the top coat on. I found even when you use the Gelish nail color it's still wet even after UVing them 4 minutes...2 minutes for each coat. It's really easy to use (and believe me I was petrified to start!!!) I also recommend one hand at a time<br />1) File the shape of your nail (or in my case put the tip on and file it down)<br />2) Use a cotton ball or small cut paper towel to use the blue liquid Nail Surface Cleanse over each nail<br />3) Use the pH Bond on each nail<br />4) Place a thin coat of Foundation on each nail and the tip of the nail....then UV light them for 2 minutes...once done saturate a cotton ball with 91% rubbing alcohol (I bought mine at CVS) and rub all your nails and the end of the nail with<br />5) Place one coat of polish over your nail and the tip of your nail and either let it dry (if using regular nail polish) or use the UV light for 2 minutes for gel polish<br />6) Place a second coat of polish over your nail and the tipand either let it dry or use the UV light for 2 minutes<br />7) Place a thin coat of the Top It Off on your nails and tip of your nails and UV light for 2 minutes<br />8) Using a cotton ball, soak it with 91% rubbing alcohol and rub it all over your nail and the tip of your nail<br />9) Switch hands and repeat #1-8....it's amazing how shiny and smooth your nails are afterwards.<br /><br />To remove the gel, saturate a cotton ball with the pink solution Artificial Nail Remover and put directly on nail, wrap it with a piece of tin foil...NOTE: Pre-making these so you don't have to keep cutting them up is priceless. Set the timer for 15 minutes and sit and wait. Once 15 minutes passes twist the cotton ball/tin foil off and use a wooden nail stick. File the nail down slightly and repeat on the other hand. Once done, repeat #1-9 above.<br /><br />Some notes I learned....rather than keep buying the Artificial Nail Remover just buy pure acetone...it's so much cheaper. Also, when deciding on a color look at the color on the bottle. It's pretty true to color. I asked the Sally's attendant for Gossip Girl (a nice dark pink color) and she gave me Good Gossip (red glittery color)....after that costly mistake I realized there were two Gossips and went back and bought the correct one which is quite nice.<br /><br />I definitely like this product and will continue using it.

  408. I am not a manicurist, but I've wathed my manicurist applying gel polish on my nails enough times that I figured I could save money and do it myself. I found some really good instructions and I have had my gel polish on for 3 days now. They still look perfect through two nights of bartending at my part time and three days of typing at my full time job. Through days of banging them on bottles, digging in the change drawer, spilling alcohol on them, washing them excessively, or typing as much as I do..no chips or peeling paint yet! Perhaps the Gelish brand had something to do with that because my manicurist uses something else that doesn't last.<br />These bottles are very small, like a sample kit. The kit runs $45-50 in stores and it was $27 when I bought it on Amazon. The ingrediants on the bottles let me know that I don't really need all of these things when I start replacing them. The top coat and foundation are the exact same thing. The nourish is just overpriced cuticle oil. The PH is just acetone. The soak off is just acetone. And the nail cleanser is just acetone. I can get less expensive options for most of these and just invest in a large bottle of top coat/foundation with colors.<br />Amazon sells many colors for around $12 for regular polish sized colors, whereas Sally's sells the tiny bottles for $14! I got lucky and found a clearance color at Sally's for $10, but it was still a tiny bottle. Inthe future, I'll order in advance from Amazon when I want a new color.<br />These are the instructions I followed.<br />1. Remove old polish and use the cleanser w/ a lint free pad to clean off the nail. (If you use a cotton ball or something linty, it will show up later on your dried nail). Push back cuticles.<br />2. Using a block buffer file, buff off the nail's natural shine and shape the nails.<br />3. Paint on the PH (which is acetone so it just vanishes off immediately).<br />4. Apply a thin coat of the foundation, which is a gooey clear polish. Cure in the light based on the times on the box (1 minute for my UV light). It will be very tacky and sticky once cured. Use a paper towel or a lint free pad and wipe off the excess until it's smooth, you will need to apply some pressure but do not touch the surface with anything else.<br />5. Apply the first thin coat of color gel polish and cure under the light per the box. (for my uv light and a dark color polish it was 3 minutes). Do not touch the polish, it will be sticky and will ruin the finish.<br />6. Repeat step 5<br />7. Apply the Top Coat the same way as the Foundation in step 4, including wiping it off after curing.<br />8. Apply Nourish oil around the cuticle beds.<br />I followed those steps to a T and my nails look better than I've ever seen them before. I will be saving a lot of money!

  418. OMG!!! Never ever thought I would be able to give myself a professional looking manicure but Gelish has changed that for me. I actually look forward to doing my nails and it's all because of Gelish. This stuff is AMAZING, anyone that is having issues with this system has to be doing something wrong with applications. I have used the Gelish system mainly with ibd gel polishes which they work AMAZING together and I have even used normal polishes making the \\"Gelly Sandwich\\" with no issues. The mani does last 2-3 weeks when using all Gel Polish and my \\"Gelly Sandwich\\" mani's last at least 2 weeks if not longer.<br /><br />The system is EASY to use and I swear maybe it's just me BUT it seems so much easier to paint the nails with Gel Polishes. I think because it's thicker and has that tacky feel but seriously you can't mess this up unless you get too close to the cuticle bed or don't clean the polish up from side of the nails before it sets. I always have an issue painting my right hand because I'm a righty, I had NO issues, no mess my right hand comes out very neat and pretty each mani.<br /><br />I see people complaining about peeling and chipping but that has to do with the application itself not the product. No disrespect but you MUST follow the rules properly. Gel Polish goes on THIN and each coat must be cured COMPLETELY before applying another coat. One of the most IMPORTANT things to remember when applying which helps avoid the lifting and peeling is that each coat covers from right above the cuticle bed to the very TIP TOP of the nail. Gel Polish works almost as an adhesive, so when you move the brush up to the top of the nail you MUST cover the very tip, almost as if you are going to paint behind the nail. Make sure the Top Coat can stick to the nail so be sure to leave a smidge of the nature nail exposed by the cuticle as well so it can stick to the nature nail which would prevent lifting and peeling.<br /><br />Each coat of polish, Foundation, Color, Color and finish with Top Coat must be dried before applying the next coat and each coat should be THIN. The Gel Polish is thicker and spreads, it's not like regular polish where if you don't have enough and need to get more for a coating. Normal polishes you get the uneven look but with Gel Polish it doesn't show, it all BLENDS together as one coat so no need to worry you don't have enough when starting each coat.<br /><br />I found it easier to apply starting in the MIDDLE of the nail and working the Polish down and up and side to side, I found this to help me avoid the extra clean up of too much polish on the sides of the nail or gathering by the cuticle's which I think gives the \\"mani from home look\\".<br /><br />I will agree with others I don't think this whole kit is a must UNLESS you are a newbie to the Gel Polish mani. Future purchases I will only be purchasing the MUST which I feel are the Foundation and the Top Coat. The extra's are nice but I agree not needed and can be purchased randomly if and when needed. The pH bond I have yet to use, the Nourishment is nice not a must but more of an everyday treatment for your cuticles, the nail polish remover I have tons of from my local dollar store. The nail cleaner which is the final step is GREAT and I do use but you can clean the nails with peroxide or alcohol that you have laying around the house. The bottles are small but don't let the size scare you, you will definitely get TONS of mani's from them.<br /><br />Lastly.... (sorry for the novel) as for light I use an LED light because it helps speed the cure time up I have found the times listed on each step to be accurate.nd finish with Top Coat must be dried before applying the next coat and each coat should be THIN. The Gel Polish is thicker and spreads, it's not like regular polish where if you don't have enough and need to get more for a coating. Normal polishes you get the uneven look but with Gel Polish it doesn't show, it all BLENDS together as one coat so no need to worry you don't have enough when starting each coat.<br /><br />I found it easier to apply starting in the MIDDLE of the nail and working the Polish down and up and side to side, I found this to help me avoid the extra clean up of too much polish on the sides of the nail or gathering by the cuticle's which I think gives the \\"mani from home look\\".<br /><br />I will agree with others I don't think this whole kit is a must UNLESS you are a newbie to the Gel Polish mani.
